# Mohawk Real End-to-End Support Matrix

This matrix records real validation evidence for `goombalab/mohawk` as of
2026-06-30. Documentation, YAML parsing, import checks, fake wrappers, and
resource-gated skips are not counted as proof that a claimed scenario works.

## Overall Conclusion

The repository is not fully validated end-to-end. The current evidence proves a
small set of dependency-light, tiny-model, public-data, and tiny CUDA/DDP/FSDP
real smokes. Tiny Mamba2/SSM fast kernels now have centralized, one-node
two-rank DDP/FSDP, and two-node four-rank DDP/FSDP GB300 training evidence.
One cached 424,303,808-parameter custom Transformers checkpoint also has
bounded GB300 generation, perplexity, lm-eval, and hidden-state visualization
evidence. A production-size 1,799,668,560-parameter Qwen2.5 hybrid now also has
real public teacher/tokenizer transfer, one verified optimizer update, and
checkpoint generation evidence. Full Mohawk training,
representative distributed or SSM training, large/gated remote datasets, gated Llama models,
and quality-trained representative Mohawk hybrid checkpoints are not currently
proven.

No public claim should describe these unproven paths as working. The only
allowed scenario statuses in this file are:

- `PASSED_END_TO_END`
- `PASSED_REAL_SMOKE`
- `FAILED_FIXED`
- `FAILED_UNFIXED`
- `BLOCKED_RESOURCE`
- `DOWNGRADED_DOCS`
- `REMOVED_OR_UNSUPPORTED`

| Fresh default venv Slurm CUDA probe, `/tmp` path | `srun -p batch -A nemotron_arch_dev --qos=interactive --gpus-per-node=4 --time=00:02:00 --immediate=1 /tmp/mohawk-phase1-default-venv-20260626/bin/python -c "import torch; ..."` | The paired `nvidia-smi -L` Slurm probe reported four `NVIDIA GB300` GPUs, but the fresh `/tmp` venv path was node-local to the login host and the compute node failed `execve()` with `No such file or directory` | `BLOCKED_RESOURCE` |
| Shared fresh default venv install for Slurm probe | `/home/abick/mohawk/artifacts/phase1_default_venv_20260626/bin/pip install -r requirements.txt` | A shared-storage fresh venv was created under ignored `artifacts/`, but the network-approved default install failed with `OSError: [Errno 122] Disk quota exceeded`; the partial generated venv was removed | `BLOCKED_RESOURCE` |
| Optional CUDA/SSM dependency manifest | `requirements-ssm-cuda.txt` | The manifest now pins the CUDA-validated Mamba 2.3 stack: `mamba-ssm==2.3.2.post1`, `causal-conv1d==1.6.2.post1`, and `quack-kernels==0.5.3`. The earlier storage venv `/home/abick/storage/mohawk/venvs/ssm-cuda-20260626` established the CUDA 13.0 source-build path and produced the causal-conv wheel with SHA-256 `cde4f4d4260aa1b857944939a6b6484d9570ea307cf728126a3828146d14b611`. A separate Python 3.12 venv created from scratch at `/home/abick/storage/mohawk/venvs/ssm-cuda-mamba23-20260630` installed the default manifest, the 349340639-byte Mamba `2.3.2.post1` aarch64 wheel with SHA-256 `e3e6115fdb969130881fff5504c20b58398bf6a200a0d3359a5ae0ab9949c70e`, causal-conv, and the declared TileLang/TVM-FFI/Quack/CUTLASS dependencies. Mohawk's `utils/__init__.py` and `components/_repo_path.py` guard kept `/home/abick/mohawk/utils` selected in that environment. GB300 jobs `748528`, `748589`, and `748805` passed fast forward/backward, real two-step `run.py` training, and generation from the resulting checkpoint. The only `pip check` failure is the pre-existing Torch platform-marker warning `nvidia-cusparselt-cu13 0.8.1 is not supported on this platform` | `FAILED_FIXED` |

The default `requirements.txt` installation story is now a validated public
runtime setup path for the non-SSM default test/evaluation surface on the login
host. A storage-backed default-runtime venv also passed tiny single-process CUDA
training, one-node two-rank DDP/FSDP training, storage-backed two-node
four-rank DDP/FSDP training, one-node two-rank DDP/FSDP
mixed-precision training, one-node two-rank DDP/FSDP bfloat16 training,
one-node two-rank DDP/FSDP checkpoint resume, two-node four-rank DDP/FSDP checkpoint resume, one-node two-rank DDP/FSDP
`eval_hstates`, `eval_ppl`, and benchmark callback smokes, and two-node
four-rank DDP/FSDP `eval_hstates`, `eval_ppl`, and benchmark callback smokes
on Slurm GB300 allocations. The same storage venv now also passes tiny
centralized, two-rank DDP/FSDP, and two-node four-rank DDP/FSDP fast
`DiscreteMamba2` training after the optional Mamba2 kernel layer is installed.
This does not prove fresh `/tmp` venv visibility on Slurm, a repo-local shared
fresh install, production hybrid configs, representative-scale multi-node SSM
training, or representative checkpoints. A current
fresh default venv under `/tmp` was not visible to Slurm compute nodes, and a
repo-local shared fresh default venv install was blocked by disk quota.

The two-node four-rank default-runtime eval callback smokes saved `Tiny-CUDA-DDP-Default-Runtime-Multinode-Eval-HStates-Smoke`, `Tiny-CUDA-FSDP-Default-Runtime-Multinode-Eval-HStates-Smoke`, `Tiny-CUDA-DDP-Default-Runtime-Multinode-Eval-PPL-Smoke`, `Tiny-CUDA-FSDP-Default-Runtime-Multinode-Eval-PPL-Smoke`, `Tiny-CUDA-DDP-Default-Runtime-Multinode-Eval-Benchmark-Smoke`, and `Tiny-CUDA-FSDP-Default-Runtime-Multinode-Eval-Benchmark-Smoke` on Slurm jobs `692419`, `692430`, `692462`, `692471`, `692475`, and `692491` with `WORLD_SIZE=4`; `eval_hstates` produced `1.5936508178710938`, `eval_ppl` produced `44002.2734375`, benchmark produced `wikitext 172057.421054`, final/latest eval hashes matched at `01292eb95b96e580140c4d7cea0215dac631811b27506d01a9d2f3daef330e55`, and benchmark final hashes matched at the same `01292eb95b96e580140c4d7cea0215dac631811b27506d01a9d2f3daef330e55` | `FAILED_FIXED` | Keep this scoped to default non-SSM login-host runtime/test validation plus storage-backed tiny single-process and DDP/FSDP CUDA, mixed-precision, bfloat16, checkpoint-resume, and eval-callback smokes; it does not prove fresh `/tmp` Slurm visibility, repo-local shared fresh install, or SSM/Mamba kernels |
| Optional CUDA/SSM dependency install | `requirements-ssm-cuda.txt` | The optional manifest pins `mamba-ssm==2.3.2.post1`, `causal-conv1d==1.6.2.post1`, and `quack-kernels==0.5.3`, and documents build-isolation and target-architecture requirements. CPU Slurm job `748228` created `/home/abick/storage/mohawk/venvs/ssm-cuda-mamba23-20260630` from an absent path, installed `requirements.txt`, then installed the cached causal-conv and Mamba 2.3 wheels with normal dependency resolution. The resulting isolated runtime uses Python 3.12.12, `torch 2.12.1+cu130`, `transformers 4.55.4`, TileLang `0.1.8`, TVM-FFI `0.1.9`, Quack `0.5.3`, CUTLASS DSL `4.6.0.dev0`, CUDA Python `13.3.1`, and Triton `3.7.1`. Mamba's cold login-host import is expensive (`147.0s` in a timed retry), but the exact Mamba2 APIs imported by `DiscreteMamba2` resolve. On a GB300, Mohawk component import took `17.742s`, selected the repository `utils`, and job `748528` produced finite bfloat16 output/input gradients with nonzero parameter gradients. Job `748589` completed two optimizer steps and saved a complete checkpoint; job `748805` generated from it. `pip check` reports only the pre-existing `nvidia-cusparselt-cu13 0.8.1 is not supported on this platform` Torch marker | `FAILED_FIXED` | Keep support scoped to Python 3.12, Torch 2.12.1+cu130, aarch64 GB300, and Mohawk's Mamba2 operators; validate source installation without the local wheel, other CUDA architectures, representative sequence lengths, multi-node Mamba 2.3, and Mamba3 kernels before claiming a portable or full Mamba3 install path |
| CUDA availability | README training requirements | Local `nvidia-smi` still fails because no NVIDIA driver is visible on the login host, direct `fla-raven` Python on the login host reports `cuda available False`, and the current fresh default venv reports `cuda available False` on the login host. Slurm interactive-QOS `nvidia-smi -L` probes report four `NVIDIA GB300` GPUs, the shared `fla-raven` Torch probe inside a Slurm step reported `torch 2.12.0+cu130`, `cuda available True`, CUDA version `13.0`, and device count `4`, and the storage-backed `ssm-cuda-20260626` default-runtime venv reported `torch 2.12.1+cu130`, `cuda available True`, CUDA version `13.0`, and device count `4` in a Slurm step. Storage-backed default-runtime tiny CUDA supervised/eval `run.py` smokes passed for centralized, one-node two-rank DDP/FSDP, and two-node four-rank DDP/FSDP training, resume, mixed-precision, bfloat16, and eval-callback paths. ## Release Readiness Gates

Before claiming full Mohawk support, the repo needs all of the following:

- A fresh install path that succeeds in a clean environment.
- CUDA-visible environment proof with real device names.
- At least one `run.py` training step on CUDA with real data/model/checkpoint
  resources.
- `torchrun`, DDP, and FSDP one-step training runs on allocated GPU resources.
- Representative/full-size mixed precision, activation checkpointing, and
  wrapper resume runs on the target distributed wrappers.
- Representative SSM/hybrid architecture runs with `mamba_ssm` and
  `causal-conv1d` installed, beyond the current tiny fast-kernel smokes.
- Real remote dataset and gated model validation, or public replacements for
  those resources.
- Representative Mohawk checkpoint lm-eval and representative perplexity evaluation.
- Executable research utility runs with declared optional dependencies installed.
